23/11/21, 21:03 - Pathi: #include <stdio.h>
#include <string.h>
#include <stdlib.h>

char ss[1001];
int mark[26] = {0};

int main(){
	int l, i;
	gets(ss);
	l = strlen(ss);
	for(i=0; i<l; i++){
		if(ss[i]>='a' && ss[i]<='z')mark[ss[i]-'a'] = 1;
		else if(ss[i]>='A' && ss[i]<='Z')mark[tolower(ss[i])-'a'] = 1;

	}


	for(i=0; i<26; i++){
//		printf("%d ", i);
		if(!mark[i])break;
	}
//	printf("\n");
	if(i==26)printf("pangram\n");
	else printf("not pangram\n");
	return 0;
}
23/11/21, 21:03 - Pathi: #include <stdio.h>
#include <string.h>
#include <math.h>
#include <stdlib.h>

int main() {
    int t;
    scanf("%d", &t);
    for (int a0 = 0; a0 < t; a0++){
        int n;
        scanf("%d", &n);
        int A[n];
        for (int i = 0; i < n; i++){
            scanf("%d", &A[i]);
        }
        int aux, permutation = 0;
        for (int i = 0; i < n - 1; i++){
            if (A[i] != i + 1){
                for (int j = i + 1; j < n; j++){
                    if (A[j] == i + 1){
                        aux = A[i];
                        A[i] = A[j];
                        A[j] = aux;
                        permutation++;
                    }
                }
            }
        }
        if (permutation % 2 == 0){
            printf("YES");
        }
        else {
            printf("NO");
        }
        printf("\n");
    } 
    return 0;
}

    for(i=0;i<size;i++)
    scanf("%d",&x[i]);
    //insertion sort..
    for(i=1;i<size;i++)
    {
        num=x[i];
        for(j=i-1;j>=0&&num<x[j];j--)
        x[j+1]=x[j];
        x[j+1]=num;

        printf("%d ",x[t]);
        printf("\n");
    }
    
}

30/11/21, 22:01 - Pathi: def check_equal_heights(heights):
    h_0 = heights[0]
    for h_i in heights[1:]:
        if h_i != h_0:
            return False
    return True


num_blocks = [int(num) for num in input().strip().split()]
num_stacks = len(num_blocks)
stacks = []
for __ in range(num_stacks):
    stack = [int(h) for h in input().strip().split()]
    stacks.append(stack[::-1])

goal = 1
best_height = 0
heights = [0] * num_stacks
positions = [0] * num_stacks
total_blocks = sum(num_blocks)
while sum(positions) < total_blocks:
    for i, stack in enumerate(stacks):
        if positions[i] == num_blocks[i]:
            continue
            
        if heights[i] == goal:
            heights[i] += stack[positions[i]]
            positions[i] += 1
        
        at_end = False
        while heights[i] < goal:
            if positions[i] == num_blocks[i]:
                at_end = True
                break
            heights[i] += stack[positions[i]]
            positions[i] += 1
            
        goal = heights[i]
            
        if at_end:
            continue
            
        if check_equal_heights(heights):
            best_height = heights[i]
            
print(best_height)

a = squares.popitem(1)

04/01/22, 20:48 - Amit Singh Hms: char* timeConversion(char* s) {
    char *st=malloc(7*sizeof(char));
    for(int i=0;i<=7;i+=1)
        *(st+i)=*(s+i);
    if(*(s+0)=='1' && *(s+1)=='2'){
        if(*(s+8)=='A'){
            *(st+0)='0';
            *(st+1)='0';
        }
        else if(*(s+8)=='P'){
            *(st+0)=*(s+0);
            *(st+1)=*(s+1);
        }
        return st;
    }
    else if(*(s+8)=='P'){
        if(*(s+0)=='0'){
            if(*(s+1)=='0'){
                *(st+0)='1';
                *(st+1)='2';
            }
            else if(*(s+1)=='1'){
                *(st+0)='1';
                *(st+1)='3';
            }
            else if(*(s+1)=='2'){
                *(st+0)='1';
                *(st+1)='4';
            }
            else if(*(s+1)=='3'){
                *(st+0)='1';
                *(st+1)='5';
            }
            else if(*(s+1)=='4'){
                *(st+0)='1';
                *(st+1)='6';
            }
            else if(*(s+1)=='5'){
                *(st+0)='1';
                *(st+1)='7';
            }
            else if(*(s+1)=='6'){
                *(st+0)='1';
                *(st+1)='8';
            }
            else if(*(s+1)=='7'){
                *(st+0)='1';
                *(st+1)='9';
            }
            else if(*(s+1)=='8'){
                *(st+0)='2';
                *(st+1)='0';
            }
            else if(*(s+1)=='9'){
                *(st+0)='2';
                *(st+1)='1';
            }
        }
        else{
            if(*(s+0)=='0'){
            *(st+0)='2';
            *(st+1)='2';
        }
            else if(*(s+0)=='1'){
            *(st+0)='2';
            *(st+1)='3';
        }
        }
        return st;
    }
    else
        return st;
}

07/01/22, 17:39 - Amit Singh Hms: def Recurgcd(a, b):
    low = min(a,b)
    high = max(a,b)
    if high%low==0:
        return low
    elif low==1:
        return 1
    else:
        return Recurgcd(low,high%low)

num1 = 12
num2 = 14
print("Given numbers are",num1,'and',num2)
print("GCD =",Recurgcd(num1,num2))

    def __init__(self, r):
        self.radius = r

    def area(self):
        return 3.14*(self.radius**2)
    
    def perimeter(self):
        return 2*3.14*self.radius

for z in range(t):
    M,N,P=[int(i) for i in input().split()]
    # print(M,N,P)
    c=0
    A=None
    Dosra=[-1]*N
    for i in range(M):
        if i+1==P:
            A=list(map(int,input().split()))
            # print(A)
        else:
            B=list(map(int,input().split()))
            # for j in range(i):
            # Dosra=[max(B[i],Dosra[i])  for j in range(N)]
            Dosra =[max(i,j) for i,j in zip(Dosra, B)]
            # print(Dosra)
    for i in range(N):
        if A[i]<Dosra[i]:
            # ans.append(Dosra[i]-A[i])
            c+=Dosra[i]-A[i]
    res=c
    # res=sum(ans) 
    print("Case #{}: {}".format(z+1,res))
    #   print('Case #{}: {}'.format(t+1,ans))

08/06/23, 14:14 - Ayush Verma: int solution(vector<int> arr, int src, int dest){
    // Two maps, visA for distance from src and visB for distance from dest
    // They serve two purpose, if visA[x] == 0, that means we haven't reached that node yet, 
    // and if it holds any value, say d, that means it is d distance away from the particular node
    map<int,int> visA,visB;
    int start = arr[src];
    int curr = 1;
    set<int> s; // contains unique set of nodes to check at last
    
    // iniitializing final nodes
    for(auto &x: arr){
        s.insert(x);
    }
    // traversing until we get to a cell where we've already reached
    while(visA[start] == 0){
        visA[start] = curr; // Marcking the distance
        curr++;
        start = arr[start];
        if(start == -1){
            break; // Getting out if we get to a node who is not pointing at any other node
        }
    }
    start = arr[dest];
    // Same logic as above but traversing from dest
    while(visB[start] == 0){
        visB[start] = curr;
        curr++;
        start = arr[start];
        if(start == -1){
            break;
        }
    }
    // This is an array of two values, vp[i].first holds the sum of distance of vp[i].second from src and dest.
    vector<pair<int,int>> vp;
    for(auto &x: s){
        if(visA[x] != 0 && visB[x] != 0){ // Checking if we ever got to that particular node from both src and dest or not
            pair<int,int> p = {visA[x] + visB[x], x};
            vp.push_back(p);
        }
    }
    // sorting and finding the node with list sum of visA[} + visB[]
    sort(vp.begin(), vp.end());
    return vp[0].second;
}

08/06/23, 14:19 - Amit Singh Hms: def largest_cycle(edges):
    result = []
    visited_from = [-1] * len(edges)
    for start_cell in range(0, len(edges)):
        cells = []
        cell = start_cell
        while cell > -1 and visited_from[cell] == -1:
            visited_from[cell] = start_cell
            cells.append(cell)
            cell = edges[cell]
        if cell > -1 and visited_from[cell] == start_cell:
            cells_idx = cells.index(cell)
            cells = cells[cells_idx:]
            if len(cells) > len(result):
                result = cells

    return result, len(result)

# Example usage:

for _ in range(size):
    edge = int(input("Enter an edge: "))
    edges.append(edge)

print("Largest cycle:", result)
print("Length of largest cycle:", result_length)

08/06/23, 14:21 - Amit Singh Hms: #python
import heapq
from typing import List

def dijkstra(graph: List[List[int]], start: int) -> List[int]:
    n = len(graph)
    dist = [float('inf')] * n
    dist[start] = 0
    heap = [(0, start)]
    while heap:
        d, u = heapq.heappop(heap)
        if d > dist[u]:
            continue
        for v in graph[u]:
            if v == -1:
                continue
            alt = dist[u] + 1
            if alt < dist[v]:
                dist[v] = alt
                # sauravhathi
                heapq.heappush(heap, (alt, v))
    return dist

def nearest_meeting_cell(n: int, edges: List[int], c1: int, c2: int) -> int:
    graph = [[] for _ in range(n)]
    for i, e in enumerate(edges):
        if e != -1:
            graph[i].append(e)
    a = dijkstra(graph, c1)
    b = dijkstra(graph, c2)
    min_dist = float('inf')
    min_node = -1
    for i in range(n):
        if a[i] != float('inf') and b[i] != float('inf') and a[i] + b[i] < min_dist:
            min_dist = a[i] + b[i]
            min_node = i
    return min_node

n = int(input())
edges = list(map(int, input().split()))
c1, c2 = map(int, input().split())
print(nearest_meeting_cell(n, edges, c1, c2))

    if visited[next_cell]:
        if cycle_sum > max_cycle_sum[0]:
            max_cycle_sum[0] = cycle_sum
    else:
        findCycle(next_cell, visited, cycle_sum)

import heapq
from typing import List

def dijkstra(graph: List[List[int]], start: int) -> List[int]:
    n = len(graph)
    dist = [float('inf')] * n
    dist[start] = 0
    heap = [(0, start)]
    while heap:
        d, u = heapq.heappop(heap)
        if d > dist[u]:
            continue
        for v in graph[u]:
            if v == -1:
                continue
            alt = dist[u] + 1
            if alt < dist[v]:
                dist[v] = alt
                # sauravhathi
                heapq.heappush(heap, (alt, v))
    return dist

def nearest_meeting_cell(n: int, edges: List[int], c1: int, c2: int) -> int:
    graph = [[] for _ in range(n)]
    for i, e in enumerate(edges):
        if e != -1:
            graph[i].append(e)
    a = dijkstra(graph, c1)
    b = dijkstra(graph, c2)
    min_dist = float('inf')
    min_node = -1
    for i in range(n):
        if a[i] != float('inf') and b[i] != float('inf') and a[i] + b[i] < min_dist:
            min_dist = a[i] + b[i]
            min_node = i
    return min_node

n = int(input())
edges = list(map(int, input().split()))
c1, c2 = map(int, input().split())
print(nearest_meeting_cell(n, edges, c1, c2))

08/06/23, 14:34 - Amit Singh Hms: def largestCycle(edges):
    result = []
    visitedFrom = [-1] * len(edges)
    for startCell in range(0, len(edges)):
        cells = []
        cell = startCell
        while cell > -1 and visitedFrom[cell] == -1:
            visitedFrom[cell] = startCell
            cells.append(cell)
            cell = edges[cell]
        if cell > -1 and visitedFrom[cell] == startCell:
            cells_idx = cells.index(cell)
            cells = cells[cells_idx:]
            if len(cells) > len(result):
                result = cells

    return result,len(result)

08/06/23, 14:34 - Amit Singh Hms: int solution(vector<int>arr){
    int ans=INT_MIN;
    int result=-1;
    vector<int>weight(arr.size(),0);
    for(int i=0;i<arr.size();i++){
        int source=i;
        int dest=arr[i];
        if(dest!=-1){
            weight[dest]+=source;
            if(ans<=weight[dest]){
                ans=max(ans,weight[dest]);
                result=dest;
            }
            
        }
    }
    if(ans!=INT_MIN)
        return result;
    return -1;
}

28/06/23, 20:59 - Amit Singh Hms: from collections import deque
def solve(arr):
    if not arr: return 0
    temp = arr.copy()
    l = temp.popleft()
    if temp[0] > temp[-1]: temp.popleft()
    else: temp.pop()
    left = l + solve(temp)
    temp = arr.copy()
    r = temp.pop()
    if temp[0] > temp[-1]: temp.popleft()
    else: temp.pop()
    right = r + solve(temp)
    return max(left, right)
def main():
    arr = deque()
    for _ in range(int(input())): arr.append(int(input()))
    print(solve(arr))
main()

28/06/23, 21:02 - Pathi: 3. Question 3

implement a prototype of a UDP network protocol

10 There is a 20 array of size nx 2, requests. At time r-requesesparos, requests [packets are to be sent over the network. The network can hold at most max packets packets in the pipeline. It delivers the data to the client at rate packets per second, i.e. rate packets are removed from the queue and delivered to the client every second.

If the number of packets exceeds max_packets at any time, the packets remaining at that time are dropped.

Given the array requests, and the integers, max_packets, and rate, find the total

number of packets that are dropped.

Example

Suppose requests = [[1, 8], [4, 9], [6, 7]], rate = 2, and max_packets=10.
Suppose requests = [[1, 8]. [4, 9]. [6, 7]], rate-2, and max packets-10.

Explanation

At t = 1.3 packets are dropped as the pipeline can only hold 7. At t = 2.2 packets are still in the pipeline and 8 more are sent. So another 3 are dropped. At t = 3.2 packets are in the pipeline and 4 more are sent. So no packets are dropped. In total 3 + 3 = 6 packets are dropped.

    ans = 0

    j = 1
    while True:
        if i == requests[j][0]:
            curr += requests[j][1]
        if curr > max_packets:
            ans = curr - max_packets
            curr -= ans
        curr -= rate
        i += 1
    return ans

    ans = 0

16/07/23, 12:10 - Ayush Verma: Melody Breakdown: 2 Days


User
A music teacher has developed a new technique to teach the students in which each unique node is identified by a lower character of English alphabet. In total there are 26 nodes in this technique from 'a to 'z. To teach a new song the music teacher first converts the song to string consisting of a to z then he breaks it into melodies. A melody is a collection of nodes in which the frequency of each node present in that melody is the same. He strictly teaches one melody in one day. You're given the song string and your task is to find and return the minimum number of days in which he can teach the whole song.

Input Specification:

input1: A string representing the song string.

Output Specification:

Return the minimum number of days in which he can teach the whole song.

Example 1:

input1: "abbaabcd"

Output: 2

Explanation:

Here the given song string is "abbaabcd" which can be broken down into two

melodies:

1. The first melody is "abbaba" where the frequency of characters a and b is equal
to 3.

2. The second melody is "cd" where the count of frequency c and d is equal to 1.
16/07/23, 12:10 - Ayush Verma: Ye ek ques ho to batana
16/07/23, 12:20 - Shobhit Tiwari: Kro pathi start
16/07/23, 12:21 - Amit Singh Hms: def minimum_days_to_teach_song(song):
    frequencies = {}
    melody_count = 0
    unique_count = 0

    for char in song:
        if char not in frequencies:
            frequencies[char] = 0
            unique_count += 1

        frequencies[char] += 1

        if frequencies[char] == len(song) // unique_count:
            melody_count += 1
            frequencies = {}

    return melody_count

16/07/23, 13:52 - Amit Singh Hms: def solve(N, A, G):
    sumg = sum(G)
    suma = sum(A)
    idx = [(i, j) for i in range(N) for j in range(i+1, N)]
    ans = float('inf')
    for i, j in idx:
        temp = (sumg-(suma-A[i]-A[j]))//(N-2)
        flag = True
        for k in G:
            if k-temp not in A:
                flag = False
                break
        if flag: return temp
    return ans

19/07/23, 21:52 - Ayush Verma: #include <iostream>
#include <vector>
#include <algorithm>

int gcd(int a, int b) {
    if (b == 0)
        return a;
    return gcd(b, a % b);
}

int findLargestMagicalGroup(int input1, const std::vector<int>& input2) {
    int maxGroupLength = 0;
    int size = input2.size();

    for (int i = 0; i < size; i++) {
        int groupLength = 1;

        for (int j = 0; j < size; j++) {
            if (i != j && gcd(input2[i], input2[j]) > 1) {
                groupLength++;
            }
        }

        maxGroupLength = std::max(maxGroupLength, groupLength);
    }

    return maxGroupLength;
}

int main() {
    int input1 = 3;
    std::vector<int> input2 = {2, 5, 10};
    int result = findLargestMagicalGroup(input1, input2);
    std::cout << "Output: " << result << std::endl;

    return 0;
}
19/07/23, 21:52 - Ayush Verma: def burst_all_balloons(A):
    N = len(A)
    time_taken = 0
    dart_power = 1
    power_factor = 1

    for i in range(N):
        balloon_power = A[i]

        while dart_power < balloon_power:
            dart_power += power_factor
            time_taken += 1

        time_taken += 1
        power_factor += 1
        dart_power = 0

    return time_taken

# Example usage:
A = [3, 5, 2, 8, 6]
print(burst_all_balloons(A))

19/07/23, 21:53 - Ayush Verma: def find_array_B(A, X):
    n = len(A)
    B = []

    for i in range(n):
        max_value = -1
        for j in range(31, -1, -1):  # Iterate from the 31st bit to the 0th bit
            if (A[i] >> j) & 1:  # Check if the jth bit of A[i] is set to 1
                if (max_value | (1 << j)) <= A[i]:
                    max_value |= (1 << j)

        X -= (A[i] & max_value)
        B.append(max_value)

    if X != 0:
        return [-1]

    return B

19/07/23, 22:11 - Shobhit Tiwari: def find_password(A, X):
    n = len(A)
    A_sorted = sorted(A)
    B = [0] * n

    for i in range(n):
        B[i] = min(A_sorted[i], X ^ A_sorted[i])

    if sum(B) == X:
        return B
    else:
        return [-1]

19/07/23, 22:22 - Ayush Verma: def distribute_string(S, M):
    if M == 1:
        return [S]

    n = len(S)
    smallest_strings = []

    for i in range(1, n - M + 2):
        sub_distributions = distribute_string(S[i:], M - 1)
        smallest_strings.extend([S[:i] + sub_dist for sub_dist in sub_distributions])

    return smallest_strings

def find_lexicographically_strongest_string(S, M):
    all_distributions = distribute_string(S, M)
    smallest_lexicographic_strings = min(all_distributions)
    strongest_string = max(smallest_lexicographic_strings)

    return strongest_string

# Example 1
input1 = 3
input2 = "good"
output1 = find_lexicographically_strongest_string(input2, input1)
print(output1)  # Output: "gd"

# Example 2
input3 = 4
input4 = "abacadae"
output2 = find_lexicographically_strongest_string(input4, input3)
print(output2) *

19/07/23, 22:23 - Amit Singh Hms: def UserMainCode(input1, input2):
    from itertools import permutations
    def divide_string(input1, input2):
        result = []
        def divide_helper(n, string, parts):
            if n == 0: result.append(parts)
            else:
                for i in range(1, len(string) - n + 2):
                    divide_helper(n - 1, string[i:], parts + [string[:i]])
        divide_helper(input1, input2, [])
        return result
    arr = []
    for i in permutations(input2):
        for i in divide_string(input1, ''.join(i)):
            arr.append(min(i))
    return max(arr)

        if i == len(input2): return 0
        return max(total%input3, r(input2, input3, i+1, total), r(input2, input3, i+1, total+input2[i]))

19/07/23, 23:04 - Amit Singh Hms: def UserMainCode(input1, input2):
    from itertools import permutations
    def divide_string(input1, input2):
        result = []
        def divide_helper(n, string, parts):
            if n == 0: result.append(parts)
            else:
                for i in range(1, len(string) - n + 2):
                    divide_helper(n - 1, string[i:], parts + [string[:i]])
        divide_helper(input1, input2, [])
        return result
    arr = []
    for i in permutations(input2):
        for i in divide_string(input1, ''.join(i)):
            arr.append(min(i))
    return max(arr)

28/09/23, 19:46 - Shobhit Tiwari: MOD = 10 ** 9 + 7

def seating_arrangements(n, p, c):
    dp = [0] * (n + 1)
    dp[0] = 1
    
    for i in range(1, n + 1):
        dp[i] = dp[i - 1]
        if i >= c:
            dp[i] = (dp[i] + dp[i - c]) % MOD
    
    result = (dp[n] - dp[n - p]) % MOD
    return result

# Input
n, p, c = map(int, input().split())

# Output
result = seating_arrangements(n, p, c)
print(result)

28/09/23, 19:48 - Shobhit Tiwari: def find_max_product(L1, R1, L2, R2):
    # Find the maximum values in each range
    max_val_1 = max(R1, L1)
    max_val_2 = max(R2, L2)
    
    # Find the minimum values in each range
    min_val_1 = min(R1, L1)
    min_val_2 = min(R2, L2)
    
    # Calculate the maximum product of a and b
    max_product = max(max_val_1 * max_val_2, min_val_1 * min_val_2)
    
    return max_product

# Input
L1, R1, L2, R2 = map(int, input().split())

# Output
result = find_max_product(L1, R1, L2, R2)
print(result)

28/09/23, 20:06 - Pathi: def seating_arrangements(n, p, c):
    # Calculate the number of chairs between each person
    chairs_between = n - p - 1

    # Calculate the number of ways to arrange the people with social distancing
    arrangements = 0

    # Iterate through all possible positions for the manager
    for manager_pos in range(n):
        # Calculate the number of chairs between the manager and the first person
        chairs_between_manager_first = (manager_pos - 1) % n

        # Calculate the number of chairs between the manager and the last person
        chairs_between_manager_last = (n - manager_pos - 1) % n

        # Check if the number of chairs between the manager and the first/last person satisfies the social distancing requirement
        if chairs_between_manager_first >= c and chairs_between_manager_last >= c:
            # Calculate the number of ways to arrange the remaining people with social distancing
            remaining_arrangements = pow(chairs_between, p - 1, 10**9 + 7)

            # Add the number of arrangements to the total
            arrangements = (arrangements + remaining_arrangements) % (10**9 + 7)

    return arrangements

# Read input from STDIN
n, p, c = map(int, input().split())

# Call the seating_arrangements function and print the result
print(seating_arrangements(n, p, c))

def solve(s1, s2):
    d1, d2 = count(s1), count(s2)
    for i, j in d1.items():
        if i in d2:
            if abs(d1[i]-d2[i]) > 3: return -1
        elif d1[i] > 3: return -1
    for i, j in d2.items():
        if i not in d1 and d2[i] > 3: return -1
    print(d1, d2)
    return min(s1, s2)

def solve(s1, s2):
    d1, d2 = count(s1), count(s2)
    for i, j in d1.items():
        if i in d2:
            if abs(d1[i]-d2[i]) > 3: return -1
        elif d1[i] > 3: return -1
    for i, j in d2.items():
        if i not in d1 and d2[i] > 3: return -1
    return min(s1, s2)

18/11/23, 10:53 - Amit Singh Hms: #include <iostream>
#include <unordered_map>

std::unordered_map<char, int> count(const std::string& s) {
    std::unordered_map<char, int> d;
    for (char i : s) {
        d[i] = (d.find(i) == d.end()) ? 1 : d[i] + 1;
    }
    return d;
}

std::string solve(const std::string& s1, const std::string& s2) {
    std::unordered_map<char, int> d1 = count(s1);
    std::unordered_map<char, int> d2 = count(s2);

    for (const auto& pair : d1) {
        char i = pair.first;
        int j = pair.second;

        if (d2.find(i) != d2.end()) {
            if (std::abs(d1[i] - d2[i]) > 3) {
                return "-1";
            }
        } else if (d1[i] > 3) {
            return "-1";
        }
    }

    for (const auto& pair : d2) {
        char i = pair.first;
        int j = pair.second;

        if (d1.find(i) == d1.end() && d2[i] > 3) {
            return "-1";
        }
    }

    return (s1 < s2) ? s1 : s2;
}

int main() {
    int n;
    std::cin >> n;

    std::string s1, s2;
    std::cin >> s1 >> s2;

    std::string res = solve(s1, s2);
    std::cout << res << std::endl;

    return 0;
}
